These are very, very good and healthy!  I used chunky applesauce instead of the oil and spiced rum instead of vanilla.  I also added about 1/3 cup honey and another 1/2 cup of oatmeal, and left out the dates.  They were SO easy and SO quick!!  They didn't make a big mess of my kitchen either; no flour or milk or whatever to spill everywhere.  I will definitely make them again!

Use parchment paper or grease pan--the banana caramelizes leaving a sticky residue.  This is my favorite kid snack recipe!

text:
This was a very good recipe. After reading the comments below I added 3 diced apples, 1/4 cup of walnuts, 1 more cup of oatmeal, 1 tsp each of cinnamon and nutmeg, used the applesauce instead of the oil, added 1/4 cup of coconut, 1/4 cup of wheat germ and 1/2 cup of honey. I also reduced the heat to 325 and the time to 15 minutes. It sounds like it was a lot more work but I found it absolutely delicious and the apples made it VERY juicy. I also greased the cookie sheet with Pam. My son (4) helped me make them and I had to put him on "time-out" for reaching onto the cookie sheet on the stove for another while I wasn't looking. I guess they're good!

text:
These are great little healthy cookie bites.  Bananas and dates make a great sweetener and if you add a bit of cinnamon, cloves, allspice (or whatever), they end up tasting like little banana bread bites.  Very good.  Very addicting.  

If you like your cookies sugar-sweet or crispy, then they aren't for you.  Sweetness relies on the ripeness of the bananas and sweetness of the dates (so they could be very sweet or only mildly so).  Cookies turn out soft.

I loved them, and will definitely make them again.

What is with all the negative reviews on this recipe?  I have been a "health nut" for many years, and this is the FIRST healthy cookie recipe that was actually good!  I did follow others' substitutions and additions: 1/2 c applesauce instead of oil Added: 1/3 c honey 1/2 c oatmeal 1 tsp. each cinnamon and nutmeg 1/4 c walnuts  The batch made 25 cookies, and here is the nutritional information that I calculated: 88 Calories 1g Total Fat 0 mg Cholesterol 1 mg Sodium 19 g Total Carbs 2 g Dietary Fiber 2 g Protein

text:
These cookies are fabulous.  Excellent as a "breakfast cookie."  I made them exactly as the recipe stated and I loved them, my mom loved them and a diabetic co-worker loved them!  I am going to try them again with some raisins and walnuts.
There are many suggestions to add sugar and chocolate chips etc, but that sort of defeats the purpose of this cookie... 
Quick, easy, healthy and a new favorite at my house.  Thanks!

An extra note...  Now that I have made over 10 batches of these in the last week, I have perfected a few things...  I use 1/2 dates and 1/2 raisins because I love raisins.  I also added a half a cup of chopped walnuts.  Once the oats have sat for 15 minutes I roll the oats into walnut sized balls and put them on the cookie sheet. Messy on the hands but turns out a nice uniform cookie.  Then once all the cookies are on the pan I squish them with a spatula.  They don't spread so you can fit lots on a pan and they come out nice and round and perfect looking.

Awesome recipe especially if you are watching your sugar.  But if not, eat them for breakfast!!

text:
After reading some of the other reviews, I decided to alter this a little bit and I am very pleased with how they turned out! I used 3 cups of rolled oats, but I ground one cup in the blender first, and used some of the oat flour to assist me in chopping the dates. (They can be very sticky when fresh!) I used coconut oil for both flavor and nutrition, and also added 1/2 cup chopped raisins and 1/2 cup mini chocolate chips, for more sweetness. I highly recommend adding 1/2 -1tsp salt! This might be why some thought the cookies tasted flat. Also a good shake of cinnamon and about 1/2 tsp cardamom. They turned out sweet enough to satisfy our family, including my 7 year old daughter, who generally hates granola bars. Baked at 325 F, convection, for about 17 minutes, until browning at the edges and on bottom. I will make these again for sure, and will experiment with other dried fruits. Very moist and snack-worthy! (:

text:
the thing about calling something a "cookie" is that people expect dessert.  To me, this is not really dessert.  It was very tasty, but in a "healthy" way, you know?  However, rolling it into a pan and making "energy bars" would conjure up a more accurate image in my mind.  

I dressed this up by subbing peanut butter for the oil.  I added an egg for cohesion, and chopped pecans and choco chips for taste.  I did add salt, because I could see how bland it would be without it.  You just don't realize what salt does to the taste of a cookie!

I will make these again, as I see plenty of options and potential as healthy energy food for my hiking and biking.  I envision dried cranberries, coconut, bran, wheat germ, etc.

text:
Wow, so happy to have a vegan cookie that even my teen daughter and her friends like!    I'm not giving this recipe 5 stars because it's the best cookie I've ever eaten, but it is a great way to cure the cookie craving without white flour, white sugar, eggs or dairy!  Very good in it's own category.  I followed one reviewer's advice and ground half of the oats to try to improve the texture.  I did use oil, and the cookies were not crumbly or difficult to work with at all.  Adding a pinch of salt and your favorite spice is a must. I also added walnuts which, in my opinion, are very important to give some crunch and improve on the gooey, oatmeal-ish texture of the cookie.  I also think the dates are a very important ingredient for sweetness and texture, and don't think other dried fruits would give as good of a result.  There have been lots of comments on how long to bake the cookies, but honestly, it didn't seem to matter much to me.   Some I cooked much longer than others, but they all turned out moist. The recipe made about 20 cookies for me.    Thank you so much for sharing this healthy treat!  They're almost gone already.

text:
These were surprisingly good. They're what I would consider a breakfast cookie and naturally ...and lightly, sweet. Like others, I replaced the oil w/ unsweetened applesauce, used about 1/3 rainins/craisins in place of dates as well as adding 1 sm apple chopped. In addition, I added about 1/4 cup chocolate chips. I wasn't sure they would hold their shape, but w/ a bit of pressing together, they did. Baked at 325F for 15 min. They were soft, chewy...and my chldren LOVED them. Yay! a healthy cookie that they'll eat! They're moist, so I wouldn't let them sit in a container for more than a few days or I suspect they'll mold. However, mine didn't last more than 24 hrs. ;) Will definitley make mulitiple times over. :)

text:
Amazingly sweet and addictive, esp. for such a healthy dessert. I agree they are not the crunchy, crispy cookie type. Instead, they're moist, soft, and chewey. I changed the recipe for 1 dozen cookies, but used the same amount the spices: 1/2 cup very ripe mashed banana (1 large banana), 3/4 cup rolled oats or other rolled grains (I used mixed triticale, oat, and rye flakes), 1 Tbsp oil, 1/3 cup mixed chopped dried apricots and dates, 1 tsp vanilla extract, 1 tsp ground ginger, and 1 tsp ground cardamom. The ginger really brought out the sweetness of the bananas and was a nice break from the usual cinnamon/nutmeg combination. I also threw in some chopped nuts, but they didn't seem to add much as the oats are already chewey and crunchy. Mine only took about 17-18 min to bake.

Loved it - reminds me of banana bread bites... only reminded me of a cookie in shape only.  I read the reviews and I have to add - QUIT thinking these are cookies. Do not bring a platter of them to a party, do not make them for your bakesale and by all means do not bring these to a cookie exchange. The lack of sugar, flour and fat should be an indication that you will be setting yourself up for disappointment.  If you want cookies, make cookies with all the fat and sugar you want. If you are looking for a healthy breakfast or snack alternative these were delish!! I subbed 1/2 cup dried chopped dates for fresh that I further chopped in my processor. I also subbed 2.5 TB coconut oil for the veg oil and added 1 tb of triple seed mix (hemp, chia, flax) & a shake of cinnamon. I cannot wait to make these "bites" again.

Well, after being on a super strict diet, these cookies tasted absolutely fantastic to me. Mind you I had been deprived of anything even remotely close to being called a cookie for about a month. Overall, I think its a great snack cookie that you can't feel to guilty about eating!!

text:
Omigosh, I love these cookies!    Just like everyone else, I did make a couple tiny changes, but I can't say for sure if that had an effect on the final product.  With modifications, it's a 4.5.  Without, it's a 4.    First, I pureed the dates in with the oil (I used olive oil) and banana.  I also added in nutmeg, cloves, and cinnamon, and chopped walnuts.  Finally, in regards to the "gummy" comments, I added in some baking powder.  (I 1/3'd the recipe, and therefore used 1/4 tsp of baking powder.  For the full recipe, you'll want to use 3/4 tsp baking powder.)    Mine weren't gummy a-tall!  They were dense, but moist, slightly sweet, nutty, banana-y, chewy, and fantastic.  Not cakey.  They are not sweet, just for fair warning.  I put a drop of agave on one when I served it to my Amor.  They were like mini banana-bread cookies.    I definitely recommend these.

text:
These cookies were good, but need a few additions. This is a good base recipe to begin with and get creative. I did the following-  1) Added  cinnamon, as suggested by so many reviewers - it's a must.  2) I added coconut flakes to half the batch and compared with/without. (1/4 cup) I think it is a lovely addition! 3) A little honey helps too. (2tbsp) * tip* these were very sticky and even though I used parchment paper, they still stuck to it. I found the key was to move to a cooling rack immediately after removing from oven. With the few additions, they've become a crowd pleaser in my home. Thanks for sharing!

If I could give it 6 stars, I would! It's absolutely awesome. I finally found a dessert that I can make that's healthy! I used REALLY ripe bananas and it actually was too sweet even though I didn't add any sugar. The dates were sweet as well so next time I won't use as ripe of the bananas. I also don't use oil so I used home made apple sauce instead. The downside of these cookies is that they are very high maintainance. It takes a while to spread on a cooking sheet making sure they are round (they come out just as you spread them). Also, it takes LOTS of time and patience to get them off the sheet without breaking them. You probably won't have that problem if you use oil instead of apple sauce. I don't use oil so I will continue using apple sauce - it's totally worth it!

extremely healthy and very versatile recipe... I had to make a lot of alterations the first time I made this. Here they are: used applesauce instead of oil, 1/2 teaspoon of cinnamon and nutmeg, 1/4 cup of coconut flakes, 1 small diced apple, two handfuls of roasted peanuts, 1/2 cup of raisins, 1/4 cup of honey, 3 cups of oats, 2 ripe bananas, and 1 T of milk. I feel like I created a whole new recipe that's why I'm giving it 3 stars.  To me it just tasted like granola and not much like a cookie. The consistency was a a tad bit rubbery. The batter was delicious and the cookie was okay. Be aware that the cookies are impossible to shape into balls and they also fall apart. It would be better if you put them in a pan and made granola bars. I don't think I'll  be making these in the future.

text:
I love these cookies. They're almost like chewy granola bars. I think this recipe is a good base. You can pretty much add whatever you want into it. I usually add chopped walnuts, raisins, and cinnamon. I'm sure any dried fruit would be fine. Next time I will try craisins and almonds. I've also made these with chopped pieces of apple and applesauce as well, and they turned out great.  I also don't put any oil in it because it just makes it greasy. I make them into really small round bite sizes by rolling in a small ball and squishing flat with my palms. Then, I bake them at 300 degrees for about 15 minutes. These don't flatten out when you bake them. They stay the same size, so you don't have to worry about leaving spaces between each cookie.

But I do think that this is a very versatile recipe that has a tremendous amount of potential for adding ingredients per your liking. Definitely things like cinnamon, allspice, nutmeg, pieces of dried fruit, nuts/seeds, fresh chopped apples, pears, peanut butter, and even chocolate or carob would make this a very healthy and quite tasty treat. Both my kiddos kept asking for more! Thank you for a wonderfully healthy cookie recipe for my family!

text:
I love how guilt-free these are... although I added a little guilt ;) I'm sure this recipe would have been fine on it's own,  but maybe a little bland. These taste to me a bit like a granola bar type cookie. So, if you're looking for a fix for your sweet tooth, you won't find it here- think HEALTHY. I have a hard time not changing recipes, so here is what I did: added 1/2 C. flaked coconut (sweetened), 2 T. ground flax seeds, 1 C. semi-sweet choc. chips & 1/2 C. toasted chopped walnuts, 1 teaspoon cinnamon; I also reduced the oil a bit and added some applesauce to make up the difference. The cookies LOOKED like they had more chocolate than they really did because of the dark date pieces. Next time I might try adding some peanut butter and mini chips instead of the regular choc. chips, that sounded good. They don't crumble too badly, just a little on the edges if the cookie isn't shaped properly prior to baking.

Not something I would personally eat, but my  1-1/2 yr old seemed to enjoy them (as well as our shih-tzu). They are a great on-the-go snack/breakfast for a busy toddler!

text:
I liked these a whole lot more than I expected to and was not expecting to leave a 5 star review. I am not big into health food, but these are yummy. I did of course make them a little less healthy, by adding 1/2 cup of chocolate chips and 1/2 a cup of walnuts in place of the dates, but still these are good for you. I also added a few heaping tablespoons of peanut butter which I may increase next time to give them more protein and a peanut butter/ banana taste. Other reviewers have mentioned this but I didn't read them before making: these cookies will not spread AT ALL so flatten them out before you put them in the oven. Oh and also...my banannas were not ripe, so I called my mom to ask her what to do. She told me to put them in the microwave. I did, for about 45 seconds or so. It worked great and they mashed easily!  I'll be sending these to my little sister at college, and hopefully they'll be a good study snack for her.

text:
These are amazing! Like most cooks on allrecipes.com, I couldn't help but modify the recipe, since I thought that the amount of oil suggested was too much and the dates' sweetness would take away from the banana's flavor.  I used 3 very ripe bananas, 1/3 cup small blueberries, 1 1/3 cups rolled oats, 1/2 cup quick oats, 1 teaspoon real vanilla extract, 1 teaspoon grapeseed/ extra virgin olive oil, 1 teaspoon honey, pinch of sea salt. I cooked them at 325F for 20 minutes on a greased pan (the first batch was hard to take off the greased foil). I like to get them as they're just starting to brown underneath. These are best hot out of the oven, and are meant to stay soft and chewy, so the term "cookie" is a little misleading.  I made a small batch without salt or honey or oil and they still came out wonderful and tasty! How's THAT for a healthy cookie? =) But keep in mind, I've been eating a very healthy diet for the last half year so my taste buds are very happy with less salts and sugars.

text:
The cookies aren't bad, but could use a little tweaking. I had trouble getting mine to harden/get past the original doughiness. They weren't bad as gooey, slimy balls, but were a little messy and left hands sticky. 

They were a little bland and the amount of dates was a little overwhelming. Next time I'm going to use half the amount of dates called for, add a little more vanilla, and a pinch of salt. 

I also used organic rolled oats which I think didn't soak up as much moisture as generic oatmeal. Next time I will try Quaker instant oatmeal with the hope of cutting back on the moisture factor. 

I like the simplicity of this recipe and definitely approve of using fruit rather than sugar to sweeten. Good idea, I just think I need to adjust it to meet my own personal preferences.

I will definitely be making these again.  A great guilt free snack or breakfast option.

I love to make this when I'm trying to eat healthy and I have some over-ripe bananas that I need to use. I do make a couple of variations based on personal taste. There are tons of ways you can change up this recipe to make it your own. I'm glad I found it... it's definitely a keeper!

text:
I'm giving this recipe 4 stars because I had to make some adjustments to make this a 5 star recipe.  I made this recipe TWICE and think I have finally perfected it:

1) Instead of oil, use 2 lunchable size applesauce (per other reviewers, thank you!)
2) use 2 cups oats and 1 cup low fat granola for more crunch, because this cookie is very soft.
3) for my personal preference, I added a diced apple, raisins, 1/4cup walnuts for more flavor and texture since I don't like dates.
4) bake at 350 for 30 minutes...I shaped my cookies into normal sized cookies, so they needed longer baking but trust me its worth it!

Overall, this recipe is a great foundation and very easy to tweak to your own liking! Love this recipe, I will always use it :) My boyfriend who doesn't like to eat "healthy" actually devoured these cookies!

We really liked this cookie.  I did substitute walnut oil for the vegetable oil and I also added 2/3 cup ground flax and an additional 1/3 cup oatmeal.   With these changes my cookies ended up crispy on the bottom and soft and chewy in the middle; the way we like them.  If you like a real crispy cookie, I wouldn't add the additional ingredients the way I did.   My cookies only took about 15 minutes to bake.  I'm thinking next time I may bake them as bars instead of cookies.   I really like this recipe as it is so flexible and easy to change to your family's likes and dislikes.   BUT, again, these are a healthy cookie so don't expect anything real sweet.   Thank you for sharing, K, I'll be making these often!

text:
Very yummy and way healthier than regular cookies! I agree with one reviewer-- these are not the typical dessert type cookies. However, that being said, they still turn out pretty sweet without any additional sugar. I did the following: used total of 3 cups of rolled oats, 1 tsp cinnamon, 1 tsp nutmeg and 1/4 tsp cloves and substituted oil with 1/3 c homemade applesauce (recipe on allrecipes: apple sauce). YUMMY! PS- the more ripe the banana, the sweeter the cookie. Next time I plan on using a green banana and see how that tastes!

text:
I'm giving these cookies four stars because I made revisions based on other reviews. I mashed three bananas, stirred in 2.5 cups of oats, 1/3 cup of honey, 1/3 cup of cinnamon apple sauce, 1 diced apple, 1 teaspoon vanilla extract, 1 teaspoon of nutmeg, and 1 teaspoon of salt. Next I lined a baking tray with wax paper, sprayed it with Pam (the first batch I didn't spray Pam and they were a pain to get off without having the paper baked on the cookie), and shaped my cookies on the sheet (they don't spread as other reviewers noted). Baked at 350 for 20 minutes produced soft, chewy, delicious cookies. As you can see from the photo I made small cookies for a company potluck, the reviews were great.

I love these cookies!  I followed suggestions and used applesauce instead.  I  made two batches; in both I added about two heaping tablespoons of peanut butter when mashing the bananas (so yummy!)! In my second batch, I didn't add the cranberries at all, and added a bit more peanut butter.  Thanks to Elvis Presley for the amazing peanut butter/banana idea!

Great cookies.  I make them very often, vegan, gluten and wheat free, no added sugar.  Can even eat them for breakfast, dessert or snack.  So easy and inexpensive.  Couldnt ask for a better cookie.  I also add 1 tbsp flax seed in 3 tbsp or so of water in the blender then mix into the recipe as this acts as a binder and they can come apart after cooking without this. These are great cookies! I used dried strawberries instead of dates and 1/2 of apple sauce instead of the oil, so I made them even healthier! They are very nice and smooth; they just don't look or taste like a regular cookie, so cookie lovers will be disappointed, like my wife and kids. I think that many cookie lovers expect either a chocolaty or sugary taste, and these will be left with the feeling that something is missing. But I am amazed that you can actually fix cookies without butter, flour, shortening and, most amazingly, sugar! These are actually good for you!!! You can eat them not only without a guilty feeling, but knowing that these are good for your health: full of vitamins and antioxidants!

I have to say, I was impressed. My son is a diabetic and has sworn off sweets. He was a sweet lover. The carbs and sugar content in here is doable. MAKE THESE COOKIES!  Easy, easy, easy -- and deeelicious!  :)  And VEGAN.  Oh, did i mention EASY?  I made some minor changes:  I ground the dry oats first, in the blender.  I halved the recipe.  Don't do this, if you don't have to.  I used raisins instead of dates (only 'cuz i didn't wanna use up my dates; and i used about half the amount of raisins that half the recipe called for -- it was plenty; if using dates, that may be different).  And i greased the cookie sheet first (because someone had recommended it).  It yielded 12 cookies.  I measured the cookie dough at approx. 1 Tbsp.  AND i flattened the cookies out before baking, per someone's recommendation.  Easy, easy.. and lots of suggested variations from other members on here.  I will make these again.  THANK YOU!!!

text:
Egg-free, dairy-free, oil-free, and almost fat-free (if you used applesauce)!This is probably the healthiest cookie recipe in the entire world.  Here are some changes I made: 1/3 cup applesauce instead of oil, 3/4 cup raisins instead of the dates, and I added 5 tsp. of honey. I made about 17 cookies 3-inch in diameter, and they come up to around only 90 calories each with no fat at all!! If you're a health freak, you'll love 'em, but I don't suggest offering it to anyone else because it does taste a little rubbery/not-so-cookie-like. The bananas were a little bit too much (I used 3 medium) so next time I think I'll use 2 and a half. Also I will try adding cinnamon and peanut butter! Great recipe, thanks so much for sharing.

text:
I am giving this recipe five stars because it is a great recipe to build from.  Even if you add little things you aren't supposed to (like sugar or chocolate chips) it's still much healthier than many of the other cookies out there.  It isn't meant to taste like a sugary treat (obviously) so think of them more as slightly sweet fruity oat bars...lol.    These were the changes I made to the recipe: *I used two bananas instead of three.  I only had two or else I would have used all three. *I diced up a small granny smith apple in place of the dates. *I used a 1/2 cup more of rolled oats. *I added a tsp of cinnamon. *I added a little less than a 4th of a cup of honey. (I would guess) and finally *I added three tablespoons of chunky peanut butter. I really enjoy these cookies as a healthy snack.  You can do so many different things with this recipe.  It keeps me from digging into the Oreos or other junk food goodies that are brought into the house.

text:
These cookies are virtually flavorless -- the banana flavor is ever so mild and there is very little sweetness to the cookie.  The only reason I am giving this 4 stars is because my toddler LOVES them, which makes me a happy mom considering how good these cookies are nutritionally.  I omitted the dates and added a cup of finely ground walnuts instead.  I also filled a 1/3 cup measuring cup about halfway with unsweetened applesauce and then topped it off with canola oil.  Next time I will add flaxseed and wheat germ to increase the nutritional value even further.  These cookies do not spread, so be sure to drop enough dough to make the cookies the size you want them once baked.

Very easy to make.  Here are the changes I made:  4 bananas, 3 diced apples, 1/2 cup toasted pecans, 1 cup applesauce, 2 tbsp melted butter, 1 tsp cinnamon, 1/2tsp nutmeg, 1/4tsp allspice, 1/2cup honey, 1/4 cup coconut, 1/4cup flaxmeal.  I baked one batch as listed above and the kids would not eat them.  Even after I let them cool before putting another in the oven.  I think it was a texture thing, they like all the ingredients seperately, but not in this combo.  I added chocolate chips to the rest of the mix and they ate a few of those.  This does taste very sweet even with out the chocolate chips.  I do miss the little crunch from other cookies.  I do not think I will make them again simply because it is not healthy for me since I am the only one eating them!

You will feel very tempted to add sugar in because that's exactly whats missing and it will taste very much so. I resisted adding any though, since they are supposed to be 'healthy', hence the naming. Don't expect these to miraculously taste like the regular sugar enriched cookie because they're not. They would definitely appeal to people who are used to sacrificing some taste for lower calorie foods. Otherwise, they're really not intended to be baked to satisfy the taste buds. However, I did find it pretty hard to stop popping them into my mouth! This recipe REALLY produces 36 cookies! Mine were about 1.5" wide. Preferred them a bit less soft so I liked the batch I baked for 35 minutes the best. Overall, liked this recipe because its really simple, easy and for healthy cookies, they're really not half bad at all.

EDIT: I made these again and completely followed the recipe (no maple syrup, no extra dried fruits, specified amount of oil) and they turned out perfect. No burning and they baked in20 minutes. 

These cookies were slightly bland,burned on the bottom halfway through baking, and never firmed up and took way longer than the specified baking time.I used half a cup of dates and added chopped apricots and dried cranberries. I added 2 tablespoons of maple syrup (and ommited some of the oil so it wouldn't be mushy-which didn't work).They taste much better cold that hot out of the oven and lasted for almost a week in the fridge. When I make these next time, I'll double the amount if spices and add a small amount of flour to prevent them from burning again.

text:
I halved the recipe as I was making them for myself. I substituted the oil for half apple sauce and half pure peanut butter. I also replaced half of the dates with chopped 76% dark chocolate, and added a teaspoon of cinnamon. 
I got 10 big 'cookies' out of this, although may have overcooked them slightly as they turned out more chewy than soft and chewy. I also worked out the calorie and sugar content per cookie (for the halved recipe plus added/substituted ingredients) and calculated it as 130 kcal and 11g sugar. So these definitely aren't healthy when it comes to sugar content!   Of course if I'd stuck with the oil or used all peanut butter in place of the oil, or replaced all of the dates with dark chocolate, this would have drastically reduced the amount of sugar to around 4.3g per cookie, which is about 1 tsp and 11g+ less than a traditional cookie of the same size. I think next time I will try that as these don't taste all that sweet to me anyway considering! 
However, they are definitely more nutritional than traditional cookies. I quite liked them as a satisfying alternative when I'm trying to be healthier.

text:
Anything that is supposed to be healthful catches my attention.  I cannot have too much sugar or fat and am always looking for some kind of baked goods that I can enjoy.

I cut the recipe in half for the first try; got 16 cookies.  I substituted chopped walnuts for half the dates and used only 1/3 the oil, substituting equal parts applesauce and fat-free plain yogurt for the rest.  I also added a little cinnamon.

These came out very chewy--not in itself a bad thing, but I had hoped for just a little more crunch.  I froze them and like to nibble on one straight out of the freezer.   This may sound crazy, but it makes a cookie last longer for me.  I will make them again.

I think raisins would work just as well as dates.

text:
I added frozen blueberries after the dough was ready. The trick is to put them in while frozen so they don't get too runny as they bake. If making two batches, put dough in freezer to keep berries frozen, and just add 2-3 minutes to cooking time. If blueberries are large it may take a little longer. I used nutmeg instead of cinnamon as nutmeg and blueberries are a great match.

3rd time I've made these, and I've made modifications each time for my personal preferences. This time I used 3/4 cup of dried cranberries instead of figs, 1/3 cup of plain Greek yogurt instead of vegetable oil, and added 3/4 cup of chopped pecans. I love how they turned out. text:
After reading the comments here, I replaced the dates with peeled, chopped Granny Smith apples (1.5 small apples per recipe), added 6 oz of chocolate chips and 1/3 cup chopped walnuts.  I made one batch with oil and another batch with apple sauce to see the difference.
What surprised me the most was that the batter doesn't hang together well when spooning out for baking. Of course, there is no flour or egg in the recipe, so that shouldn't be surprising. 
My batch with applesauce hung together better than the one with oil. 
Both batches tasted really good to me, and very little different  from each other. In fact, they tasted so good  I ate way too many of them and gained a pound or so. Since I made them as a healthier alternative to sugary holiday cookies, I didn't completely meet my goal.  LOL.
The cookies after cooling were very moist, to the point that they didn't hold together well in a storage tub as individual cookies, they were more like moist granola macaroons. They were so moist, in fact, that I worried that they might require refrigerated storage. 
If I made them again, I'd reduce the chocolate chips down to 3 oz per batch and the chopped walnuts down to 1/4 cup.
I'm still looking for my perfect low sugar oatmeal chocolate chip cookie.  I appreciate AllRecipes for always including nutritional information on all of the recipes.
My recipe made about 50 small cookies. I calculated the following nutritional information. (Sorry, I left out the fat calculation.)
Calories:

text:
Wow! This recipe has really been beaten up for a high expectation level it would be the perfect oatmeal "cookie". The word "cookie" is more symbolic, it is a sweet treat you can grab like a cookie BUT... you have to appreciate it as a healthy alternative. First of all, your bananas HAVE to be really ripe and soft; almost mushy. The bananas offer plenty sweetness, and yes, you need to like bananas to enjoy this recipe! Also, Please do not use steel cut oats. I have been making baked oatmeal for years changing flavors, nuts and dried fruits. I thought this sounded like a nice change and it exceeded my expectations! I used melted coconut oil for the oil and raisins for the fruit and had to put them away to stop eating them! In the future I will perhaps use applesauce or nut butter, adding spices and nuts and changing up the fruit, however, I am very happy to have found this recipe I can adapt and make my own with time. Thank you, K. Gailbrath, for sharing!

Not the worst no-refined sugar dessert I've tried.  I did add some cinnamon and nutmeg to the mix.  I chose no added sugar applesauce instead of vegetable oil.  The taste was not bad...I would recommend using very ripe bananas to add to the sweetness of the cookie.  Mine were a tish not quite ready, but I didn't want to wait.  The sweetness level could be improved just using very ripe bananas.  Otherwise they turned out great. As someone who is trying to cut down on sugars because I want to (an admitted taste-struggle!), I think some of the people who left negative reviews probably are hoping for something to be as extremely sweet as a refined sugar dessert. Nothing wrong with this recipe, no-sugar is just an adjustment for the taste buds.

text:
I made these with my 1 year old nephew and 3 year old niece in mind. Considering the simple ingredients and no added sugar, these were not bad.  I halved the recipe and added extra banana so I could leave out the oil.  Instead of vanilla I put in a dash of clove and nutmeg.  I baked them for 7 minutes at 325 then another 13 at 350.  They were moist and not rubbery at all.  They tasted pretty good too. The sweetness came from the banana and apricots and dates that I added.  I probably wont make these for myself but I think its a healthy treat for kids.

I must admit that when I first tried these, about an hour after baking, I was disappointed. I thought they were pretty bland. The next day-I tried them again and found them to be a really satisfying snack. We gobbled them up pretty quickly. My four year old loved them. These are not your typical oatmeal cookie so don't expect the same sweetness. I made a couple of minor changes to the recipe. I used a large jar of baby food bananas AND a large ripe banana. (I needed to get rid of the jar of baby food) I used applesauce in place of the oil and threw in a handful of walnuts since I usually enjoy that flavor combination. I will certainly be making these again and I think the next time I will try it with chopped bananas. A wonderful guilt free HEALTHY snack.

I did use raisins instead of dates b/c I don't like them, I also added a few chopped walnuts for protein.  I am a total beleiver, if you follow a recipe, it should be comparable to others feelings on it.  Recipes are easy to do!  The only thing that could have been wrong with these is if the bananas weren't enough.  Unfortunately, the recipe says 3 bananas.  That is not a measurement since bananas are differant sizes.  I have a banana bread recipe that also says 3 bananas...or 1 cup.  So, if my 3 bananas weren't what the recipe maker didn't have in mind, that is the only problem their could be.  I didn't even both making the entire batch or sharing them with my family since i couldn't even stomach the one I tried.  YUK!!!

I made these with bananas and fresh blueberries.  I was very excited to try one but I did not care for this at all.  Thank goodness I only made 24 cookies and wasted 2 bananas.  The oil amount (3 Tbsp) was excessive.  I could not get them off the cookie sheet.  I am beside myself and wish I hadn't wasted my time making these-that is how horrid these were.  Next time, I will follow my own instincts as to what I make.  I had a feeling they would be too oily and chewy-weird, but I gave them a whirl anyways.  BIG MISTAKE!!!!!!!

I used half raisins and half prunes for the dates, because that's what I had on hand, and whizzed them in the food processor to chop.
